The Ash'ari Thesis: Attributes Not Other Than Essence
Ijji states and then critiques the Ash'ari formulation on attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari claim that divine attributes are 'not other' than the essence and how this formulation avoids separating or identifying them with the essence.

Core Idea
Ash'ari attributes are neither identical nor separate from the essence.

The passage opens by stating the Ash'ari position that attributes are expressed in a way that does not imply existence—a delicate balancing act. Ijji then critiques earlier scholars for understanding 'distinctness' as implying possible separation, which leads to problems. This lesson unpacks the opening gambit.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Read the first sentence: 'Attributes from another aspect, so they expressed this known thing with that expression which has no indication of existence which was disputed.' This is the core thesis.
Note the careful wording: attributes are 'known' but not explicitly existent.
2
Identify the critique
The commentator says 'this is a statement with no dust upon it, but there is a discussion.' He then raises an issue about earlier masters' examples.
The examples involve parts of a whole or principles of predicates, not the predicates themselves.
3
Understand the misunderstanding
The commentator states that the masters understood 'distinctness' as allowing separation from both sides, which is not the intended meaning.
This misunderstanding leads to later objections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الرابع - المقصد السابع : الاثنان هما الغيران

صفات من وجه آخر، فعبروا عن هذا المعلوم، بتلك العبارة التي لا إشعار لها بالوجود الذي اختلف فيه . ( وهذا كلام لا غبار عليه وفيه بحث : لأن كلام المشايخ في أجزاء غير محمولة كالواحد من العشرة واليد من زيد كما أوردوها في تمثيلاتهم، وفي مبادئ المحمولات كالعلم والقدرة والإرادة لا في المحمولات، كالعالم والقادر والمريد . والظاهر أنهم فهموا من التغاير جواز الانفكاك من الجانبين، فأقدموا على ما قالوا. وأيضاً لما أثبتوا صفات موجودة قديمة زائدة على ذاته تعالى، لزمهم كون القدم صفة لغير الله تعالى، فدفعوه بذلك . وأيضاً لزمهم أن تكون تلك الصفات مستندة إلى الذات، إما بالاختيار فيلزم التسلسل في القدرة والعلم والحياة والإرادة، ويلزم أيضاً كون الصفات حادثة، وإما بالإيجاب فيلزم كونه تعالى موجبا بالذات، ولو في بعض الأشياء، فتستروا عن هذا بأنها إنما تكون محتاجة مستندة إلى علة إذا كانت مغايرة للذات .

قوله : (كون الصفات إلخ) لما تقرر عندهم من أن فعل المختار لكونه مسبوقاً بالقصد والاختيار يكون حادثاً، وإن خالف فيه الآمدي. قوله تعالى موجباً بالذات فلا يكون الإيجاب نقصاناً، فجاز أن يتصف به بالقياس إلى بعض مصنوعاته، ودعوى أن إيجاب الصفات كمال وإيجاب غيرها نقص مشكلة . قوله : ( فتستروا عن هذا إلخ لا يخفى أن التستر ينافي جعلها من الاعتقاديات، والذي عندي أن ما وقع من الشيخ الأشعري: هو أن صفاته تعالى ليست غير الذات؛ لأن الغيرين

قوله : ( وفيه بحث لأن كلام المشايخ إلخ) وأيضاً الاتحاد هوية، والاختلاف ماهية ثابت في كل صفة محمولة لازمة كانت أو مفارقة مع أن الشيخ الأشعري صرح بأن المفارقة سمي أغياراً على ما نقله الآمدي . قوله : ( والظاهر أنهم فهموا إلخ ) هذا إنما يصح على ما يقتضيه ظاهر استدلالهم، من أن الصفة مطلقاً ليست غير الموصوف، وأما على ما نقله الآمدي من أن صفات الأفعال غير الموصوف عند الشيخ وعامة الأصحاب، فلا ؛ لأن جواز الانفكاك ها هنا من أحد الجانبين لا منهما معاً. قوله : ( فدفعوه بذلك ) إن كان المراد بهذا الدفع التقصي عما قاله المعتزلة، من أن إثبات القدماء كفر، فلا حاجة إليه فإن الكفر إثبات ذوات قدماء لا ذات وصفة كما مر بل الكفر إثبات تعدد الواجب. هذا، وقد نقل عن الشارح أن الظاهر أن ما ذكره يدفع قدم غير الله تعالى، لا تعدد القدماء وتكثره؛ لأن الذات الصفة، والصفات بعضها مع بعض وإن لم تكن متغايرة، لكنها متعددة متكثرة قطعاً؛ إذ التعدد إنما يقابل الوحدة .

قوله : (مستندة إلى الذات إلخ وكونها واجبة لذاتها بين الاستحالة، ولذا لم يذكره . قوله : ( ويلزم أيضاً كون الصفات حادثة إنما لم يقل : ويلزم أيضاً كونه حادثة؛ لئلا يتوهم رجوع الضمير إلى الأربعة المذكورة فإن الحدوث لازم في الصفات كلها على هذا التقدير، وإن كان لزوم التسلسل في الأربعة لا في الكلام والسمع والبصر . نعم لو ثبت التكوين يلزم التسلسل فيه أيضاً. واعلم أن لزوم حدوث الصفات حينئذ بناء على ما هو المشهور، وأما على ما ذكره الآمدي من جواز قدم أثر المختار فلا نعم يلزم في الأربعة تقدم الشيء على نفسه، أو التسلسل فليتأمل .

قوله : ( فتستروا عن هذا إلخ الظاهر أن التستر عن هذا يحصل بالقول بأن علة الاحتياج مطلقاً الحدوث، وإن لزم كلا وجهي التستر لزوم تعدد الواجب .
The Fourth Observatory - The Seventh Objective: The two are the two distinct things. Attributes from another aspect, so they expressed this known thing with that expression which has no indication of existence which was disputed. (This is a statement with no dust upon it, but there is a discussion: because the speech of the masters concerning parts that are not predicated, like the one from ten and the hand from Zayd, as they presented in their examples, and concerning principles of predicates like knowledge, power, and will, not concerning predicates like knowing, powerful, and willing. And it appears that they understood from distinctness (al-taghayur) the permissibility of separation from both sides, so they proceeded with what they said. Also, when they affirmed existing eternal attributes additional to His essence, may He be exalted, it necessitated for them that eternity is a quality for other than Allah, so they repelled that with this. Also, it necessitated for them that those attributes are dependent on the essence, either by choice, then there would follow infinite regress in power, knowledge, life, and will, and also that the attributes are originated; or by necessitation, then it would necessitate that He, may He be exalted, is a necessitator by essence, even in some things, so they covered this by saying that they are only in need of and dependent upon a cause if they are distinct from the essence. His statement: 'concerning the attributes etc.' Because it was established with them that the act of the free agent, because it is preceded by intention and choice, is originated, even though al-Amidi disagreed. His statement, may He be exalted, 'necessitator by essence' so necessitation is not a deficiency, so it is permissible for Him to be described with it in relation to some of His creations, and the claim that necessitation of attributes is perfection and necessitation of other things is deficiency is problematic. His statement: 'they covered this etc.' It is not hidden that covering contradicts making them among the beliefs, and what I have is that what occurred from al-Shaykh al-Ash'ari is that His attributes, may He be exalted, are not other than the essence; because the two distinct things... His statement: 'there is a discussion because the speech of the masters etc.' Also, union is by identity, and difference is by quiddity, established in every predicated attribute, whether necessary or separable, although al-Shaykh al-Ash'ari stated that the separable ones are called others ('aghyar) according to what al-Amidi transmitted. His statement: 'and it appears that they understood etc.' This is only correct according to what the apparent meaning of their argument requires, that the attribute is absolutely not other than the described. But according to what al-Amidi transmitted that the attributes of actions are other than the described according to al-Shaykh and the generality of the companions, then no; because the permissibility of separation here is from one side, not from both together. His statement: 'so they repelled that' If what is meant by this repelling is evasion of what the Mu'tazila said, that affirming eternal entities is disbelief, then there is no need for it, for disbelief is affirming eternal essences, not essence and attribute, as has passed; rather disbelief is affirming multiplicity of the Necessary. This, and it has been transmitted from the commentator that the apparent meaning is that what he mentioned repels the eternity of other than Allah, not the multiplicity and abundance of eternal entities; because the essence [and] the attribute, and the attributes with each other, even if they are not distinct, are certainly multiple and abundant; for multiplicity is opposed to unity. His statement: 'dependent on the essence etc.' And their being necessary by essence is clearly impossible, so he did not mention it. His statement: 'and it also necessitates that the attributes are originated' He only did not say: 'and it also necessitates that He is originated' so that it would not be imagined that the pronoun refers to the four mentioned, for origination is necessary in all attributes according to this estimation, and if regression in the four is necessary, not in speech, hearing, and sight. Yes, if creation (takwin) is affirmed, regression is necessary in it also. And know that the necessity of the origination of attributes then is based on what is well-known; but according to what al-Amidi mentioned of the permissibility of the eternity of the effect of the free agent, then [the problem] remains: in the four, precedence of a thing over itself, or regression, so let it be considered. His statement: 'they covered this etc.' Apparently, covering this is achieved by saying that the cause of need is absolutely origination, even if both aspects of covering necessitate multiplicity of the Necessary.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on the Seventh Objective, which asserts that the divine attributes are not identical to the essence (not 'the same') but also not completely separate entities. The passage begins by noting that scholars expressed the known concept of attributes without indicating the disputed existence. The commentator then addresses a discussion: the earlier masters spoke about parts that are not predicated (like a part of a whole) and about principles of predicates (like knowledge, power, will), not about the predicates themselves. They understood 'distinctness' (al-taghayur) to imply the possibility of separation from both sides. This leads to several problems: affirming eternal attributes additional to the essence would make eternity a quality of something other than God; also, the attributes would be dependent on the essence either by choice (which would cause infinite regress and imply the attributes are originated) or by necessitation (which would make God a necessitator by essence). The scholars tried to cover these problems by claiming that attributes only need a cause if they are distinct from the essence. The commentator then explains each part: 'His statement (concerning the attributes etc.)' clarifies that acts of a free agent are originated, and necessitation is not necessarily a deficiency. 'His statement (they covered this etc.)' criticizes that covering contradicts taking these as matters of belief, and mentions al-Ash'ari's view that attributes are not other than the essence. 'His statement (there is a discussion etc.)' notes that union and difference are matters of identity and quiddity, and al-Ash'ari considered separable attributes as other. 'His statement (and it appears that they understood etc.)' restricts the argument to the apparent meaning of their reasoning, while according to al-Amidi, attributes of actions are other than the described in al-Ash'ari's view. 'His statement (so they repelled that)' distinguishes between repelling disbelief (affirming multiple eternal beings) and repelling eternity of other than God. The commentator quotes al-Sharh that the repelling concerns the latter. 'His statement (dependent on the essence etc.)' notes that attributes being necessary by essence is impossible. 'His statement (and it also necessitates that the attributes are originated)' explains the careful wording to avoid confusion. The passage ends with a note that the cause of need is origination, and both ways of covering lead to multiplicity of the Necessary (which is disbelief). The overall argument defends the Ash'ari position that attributes are neither identical to the essence nor separate entities, and that the objections raised by critics are addressed.

Key Terms
التغاير
الصفات
الذات
الغيرين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ash'ari attributes are either identical to the essence or completely separate entities.
Correction: The Ash'ari position is that attributes are 'not other' in a way that implies neither identity nor separate existence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did the earlier masters understand from 'distinctness' (al-taghayur)?
A) That attributes are identical to the essence
B) That separation is possible from both sides
C) That attributes are separate entities
D) That attributes are not real

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari formulation of attributes as 'not other' is intended to avoid both identity and separation, but early scholars misinterpreted it as implying possible separation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on Allah's attributes, do you find yourself imagining them as separate 'things' attached to His essence? What does the Ash'ari formulation say about that, and how should that change your mental picture to avoid compromising His oneness?
?
Ijji critiques early masters for misunderstanding distinctness as implying possible separation. Have you ever thought about Allah's attributes in a way that unintentionally made them seem like removable parts? What specific step can you take today to ensure your belief about the attributes aligns with the Ash'ari position that they are neither identical nor separate?
?
The passage warns against assuming that distinctness implies possible separation. In your daily life, do you treat Allah's attributes—like His knowledge, power, and mercy—as if they are distinct forces operating independently or as intrinsic to His essence? How does that affect your reliance on Him and your understanding of His oneness?

The Mu'tazila Objection: Eternity of Attributes
Ijji presents the Mu'tazila objection and the Ash'ari defense against it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila objection that affirming eternal attributes implies multiple eternal beings and how the Ash'aris respond.

Core Idea
Affirming eternal attributes could imply multiple eternal beings.

The Mu'tazila argued that if attributes are eternal and distinct from the essence, then eternity becomes a quality of something other than God, leading to disbelief (affirming multiple eternal beings). The Ash'aris respond by saying the attributes are not 'other' in a way that implies separation. This lesson examines this key objection and its defense.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the passage: 'when they affirmed existing eternal attributes additional to His essence, it necessitated that eternity is a quality for other than Allah.'
This is the Mu'tazila's core argument.
2
Understand the Ash'ari response
The passage says 'so they repelled that with this.' The commentator then explains what 'repelling' means.
The response is that attributes are not 'other' in the sense of being separate entities.
3
Distinguish disbelief types
The commentator clarifies that disbelief is affirming multiple eternal essences, not an eternal attribute alongside the essence.
This is a nuanced distinction.

Attributes from another aspect, so they expressed this known thing with that expression which has no indication of existence which was disputed. (This is a statement with no dust upon it, but there is a discussion: because the speech of the masters concerning parts that are not predicated, like the one from ten and the hand from Zayd, as they presented in their examples, and concerning principles of predicates like knowledge, power, and will, not concerning predicates like knowing, powerful, and willing. And it appears that they understood from distinctness (al-taghayur) the permissibility of separation from both sides, so they proceeded with what they said. His statement, may He be exalted, 'necessitator by essence' so necessitation is not a deficiency, so it is permissible for Him to be described with it in relation to some of His creations, and the claim that necessitation of attributes is perfection and necessitation of other things is deficiency is problematic. His statement: 'they covered this etc.' It is not hidden that covering contradicts making them among the beliefs, and what I have is that what occurred from al-Shaykh al-Ash'ari is that His attributes, may He be exalted, are not other than the essence; because the two distinct things... His statement: 'there is a discussion because the speech of the masters etc.' Also, union is by identity, and difference is by quiddity, established in every predicated attribute, whether necessary or separable, although al-Shaykh al-Ash'ari stated that the separable ones are called others ('aghyar) according to what al-Amidi transmitted. His statement: 'and it appears that they understood etc.' This is only correct according to what the apparent meaning of their argument requires, that the attribute is absolutely not other than the described. But according to what al-Amidi transmitted that the attributes of actions are other than the described according to al-Shaykh and the generality of the companions, then no; because the permissibility of separation here is from one side, not from both together. His statement: 'so they repelled that' If what is meant by this repelling is evasion of what the Mu'tazila said, that affirming eternal entities is disbelief, then there is no need for it, for disbelief is affirming eternal essences, not essence and attribute, as has passed; rather disbelief is affirming multiplicity of the Necessary. This, and it has been transmitted from the commentator that the apparent meaning is that what he mentioned repels the eternity of other than Allah, not the multiplicity and abundance of eternal entities; because the essence [and] the attribute, and the attributes with each other, even if they are not distinct, are certainly multiple and abundant; for multiplicity is opposed to unity. His statement: 'dependent on the essence etc.' And their being necessary by essence is clearly impossible, so he did not mention it. His statement: 'and it also necessitates that the attributes are originated' He only did not say: 'and it also necessitates that He is originated' so that it would not be imagined that the pronoun refers to the four mentioned, for origination is necessary in all attributes according to this estimation, and if regression in the four is necessary, not in speech, hearing, and sight. Yes, if creation (takwin) is affirmed, regression is necessary in it also. And know that the necessity of the origination of attributes then is based on what is well-known; but according to what al-Amidi mentioned of the permissibility of the eternity of the effect of the free agent, then [the problem] remains: in the four, precedence of a thing over itself, or regression, so let it be considered. His statement: 'they covered this etc.' Apparently, covering this is achieved by saying that the cause of need is absolutely origination, even if both aspects of covering necessitate multiplicity of the Necessary.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on the Seventh Objective, which asserts that the divine attributes are not identical to the essence (not 'the same') but also not completely separate entities. The passage begins by noting that scholars expressed the known concept of attributes without indicating the disputed existence. The commentator then addresses a discussion: the earlier masters spoke about parts that are not predicated (like a part of a whole) and about principles of predicates (like knowledge, power, will), not about the predicates themselves. They understood 'distinctness' (al-taghayur) to imply the possibility of separation from both sides. This leads to several problems: affirming eternal attributes additional to the essence would make eternity a quality of something other than God; also, the attributes would be dependent on the essence either by choice (which would cause infinite regress and imply the attributes are originated) or by necessitation (which would make God a necessitator by essence). The scholars tried to cover these problems by claiming that attributes only need a cause if they are distinct from the essence. The commentator then explains each part: 'His statement (concerning the attributes etc.)' clarifies that acts of a free agent are originated, and necessitation is not necessarily a deficiency. 'His statement (they covered this etc.)' criticizes that covering contradicts taking these as matters of belief, and mentions al-Ash'ari's view that attributes are not other than the essence. 'His statement (there is a discussion etc.)' notes that union and difference are matters of identity and quiddity, and al-Ash'ari considered separable attributes as other. 'His statement (and it appears that they understood etc.)' restricts the argument to the apparent meaning of their reasoning, while according to al-Amidi, attributes of actions are other than the described in al-Ash'ari's view. 'His statement (so they repelled that)' distinguishes between repelling disbelief (affirming multiple eternal beings) and repelling eternity of other than God. The commentator quotes al-Sharh that the repelling concerns the latter. 'His statement (dependent on the essence etc.)' notes that attributes being necessary by essence is impossible. 'His statement (and it also necessitates that the attributes are originated)' explains the careful wording to avoid confusion. The passage ends with a note that the cause of need is origination, and both ways of covering lead to multiplicity of the Necessary (which is disbelief). The overall argument defends the Ash'ari position that attributes are neither identical to the essence nor separate entities, and that the objections raised by critics are addressed.

الصفات
الذات
الكفر

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming eternal attributes is considered disbelief (kufr) by the Mu'tazila.
Correction: The passage clarifies that belief is in multiple eternal essences, not in an attribute alongside the essence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what constitutes disbelief (kufr) regarding eternity?

B) Affirming multiple eternal essences
C) Denying attributes
D) Affirming that attributes are not other

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari response to the Mu'tazila objection is that attributes are not 'other' in a way that implies multiple eternal beings; the charge of kufr only applies to affirming multiple eternal essences.

Dependence of Attributes: Choice vs. Necessitation
Ijji presents the objection of dependence and the Ash'ari covering argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the problem of the attributes' dependence on the essence and the Ash'ari covering argument that such dependence only occurs if attributes are distinct.

Core Idea
If attributes depend on essence, they require a cause—unless they are not distinct.

A major objection against the Ash'ari view is that if attributes are distinct from the essence, they must be dependent on it either by divine choice (leading to infinite regress) or by necessity (making God a necessitator). The Ash'ari response is that dependence only applies when things are truly distinct. This lesson unpacks this argument and the commentary on it.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read: 'also, it necessitated for them that those attributes are dependent on the essence, either by choice... or by necessitation...'
Two problematic options are presented.
2
Understand the covering argument
The Ash'aris responded: 'they are only in need of a cause if they are distinct from the essence.'
This is the covering (tastur).
3
Reflect on the commentary
The commentator then discusses the problems with this covering and quotes al-Ash'ari's final position.
He notes that the covering contradicts making these matters beliefs.

المرصد الرابع - المقصد السابع : الاثنان هما الغيران

صفات من وجه آخر، فعبروا عن هذا المعلوم، بتلك العبارة التي لا إشعار لها بالوجود الذي اختلف فيه . ( وهذا كلام لا غبار عليه وفيه بحث : لأن كلام المشايخ في أجزاء غير محمولة كالواحد من العشرة واليد من زيد كما أوردوها في تمثيلاتهم، وفي مبادئ المحمولات كالعلم والقدرة والإرادة لا في المحمولات، كالعالم والقادر والمريد . والظاهر أنهم فهموا من التغاير جواز الانفكاك من الجانبين، فأقدموا على ما قالوا. وأيضاً لما أثبتوا صفات موجودة قديمة زائدة على ذاته تعالى، لزمهم كون القدم صفة لغير الله تعالى، فدفعوه بذلك . وأيضاً لزمهم أن تكون تلك الصفات مستندة إلى الذات، إما بالاختيار فيلزم التسلسل في القدرة والعلم والحياة والإرادة، ويلزم أيضاً كون الصفات حادثة، وإما بالإيجاب فيلزم كونه تعالى موجبا بالذات، ولو في بعض الأشياء، فتستروا عن هذا بأنها إنما تكون محتاجة مستندة إلى علة إذا كانت مغايرة للذات .

قوله : (كون الصفات إلخ) لما تقرر عندهم من أن فعل المختار لكونه مسبوقاً بالقصد والاختيار يكون حادثاً، وإن خالف فيه الآمدي. قوله تعالى موجباً بالذات فلا يكون الإيجاب نقصاناً، فجاز أن يتصف به بالقياس إلى بعض مصنوعاته، ودعوى أن إيجاب الصفات كمال وإيجاب غيرها نقص مشكلة . قوله : ( فتستروا عن هذا إلخ لا يخفى أن التستر ينافي جعلها من الاعتقاديات، والذي عندي أن ما وقع من الشيخ الأشعري: هو أن صفاته تعالى ليست غير الذات؛ لأن الغيرين

قوله : ( وفيه بحث لأن كلام المشايخ إلخ) وأيضاً الاتحاد هوية، والاختلاف ماهية ثابت في كل صفة محمولة لازمة كانت أو مفارقة مع أن الشيخ الأشعري صرح بأن المفارقة سمي أغياراً على ما نقله الآمدي . قوله : ( والظاهر أنهم فهموا إلخ ) هذا إنما يصح على ما يقتضيه ظاهر استدلالهم، من أن الصفة مطلقاً ليست غير الموصوف، وأما على ما نقله الآمدي من أن صفات الأفعال غير الموصوف عند الشيخ وعامة الأصحاب، فلا ؛ لأن جواز الانفكاك ها هنا من أحد الجانبين لا منهما معاً. قوله : ( فدفعوه بذلك ) إن كان المراد بهذا الدفع التقصي عما قاله المعتزلة، من أن إثبات القدماء كفر، فلا حاجة إليه فإن الكفر إثبات ذوات قدماء لا ذات وصفة كما مر بل الكفر إثبات تعدد الواجب. هذا، وقد نقل عن الشارح أن الظاهر أن ما ذكره يدفع قدم غير الله تعالى، لا تعدد القدماء وتكثره؛ لأن الذات الصفة، والصفات بعضها مع بعض وإن لم تكن متغايرة، لكنها متعددة متكثرة قطعاً؛ إذ التعدد إنما يقابل الوحدة .

قوله : (مستندة إلى الذات إلخ وكونها واجبة لذاتها بين الاستحالة، ولذا لم يذكره . قوله : ( ويلزم أيضاً كون الصفات حادثة إنما لم يقل : ويلزم أيضاً كونه حادثة؛ لئلا يتوهم رجوع الضمير إلى الأربعة المذكورة فإن الحدوث لازم في الصفات كلها على هذا التقدير، وإن كان لزوم التسلسل في الأربعة لا في الكلام والسمع والبصر . نعم لو ثبت التكوين يلزم التسلسل فيه أيضاً. واعلم أن لزوم حدوث الصفات حينئذ بناء على ما هو المشهور، وأما على ما ذكره الآمدي من جواز قدم أثر المختار فلا نعم يلزم في الأربعة تقدم الشيء على نفسه، أو التسلسل فليتأمل .

قوله : ( فتستروا عن هذا إلخ الظاهر أن التستر عن هذا يحصل بالقول بأن علة الاحتياج مطلقاً الحدوث، وإن لزم كلا وجهي التستر لزوم تعدد الواجب .
The Fourth Observatory - The Seventh Objective: The two are the two distinct things. Attributes from another aspect, so they expressed this known thing with that expression which has no indication of existence which was disputed. (This is a statement with no dust upon it, but there is a discussion: because the speech of the masters concerning parts that are not predicated, like the one from ten and the hand from Zayd, as they presented in their examples, and concerning principles of predicates like knowledge, power, and will, not concerning predicates like knowing, powerful, and willing. And it appears that they understood from distinctness (al-taghayur) the permissibility of separation from both sides, so they proceeded with what they said. Also, when they affirmed existing eternal attributes additional to His essence, may He be exalted, it necessitated for them that eternity is a quality for other than Allah, so they repelled that with this. His statement: 'they covered this etc.' It is not hidden that covering contradicts making them among the beliefs, and what I have is that what occurred from al-Shaykh al-Ash'ari is that His attributes, may He be exalted, are not other than the essence; because the two distinct things... Essential and Meaningful Attributes: Primary Definition
Sanusi defines the two types of attributes and gives examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core definitions of essential and meaningful attributes in Kalam and their key examples.

Core Idea
An essential attribute is known without adding anything; a meaningful attribute needs an extra concept.

In this passage, the author lays out the foundational distinction between two types of attributes: those that are intrinsic to the essence and those that require an additional notion. This distinction is crucial for later discussions about God's attributes. Let's explore the primary definition and examples.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once. Then read the literal translation. Focus on the two definitions given.
Notice the phrase 'without conceiving an additional matter'.
2
Identify the two types
The passage defines al-sifa al-nafsiyya and al-sifa al-ma'nawiyya. Underline the key difference: whether an additional concept is needed.
3
Examine the examples
List the examples: humanity, reality, existence, thingness for essential; spatial occupation and temporal origination for meaningful. Ask why each fits its category.
Consider why existence is considered essential here.
4
Understand the alternative phrasing
The passage restates: essential indicates essence without extra meaning; meaningful indicates extra meaning. This reinforces the definition.

الصفة النفسية ما لا يحتاج وصف الشيء به إلى تعقل أمر زائد عليه كالإنسانية، والحقيقة، والوجود، والشيئية للإنسان، وتقابلها الصفات المعنوية التي تحتاج في الوصف بها إلى تعقل أمر زائد على ذات الموصوف كالتحيز والحدوث، وبعبارة أخرى : الصفة النفسية تدل على الذات دون معنى زائد عليها والمعنوية ما تدل على معنى زائد على الذات وقال بعضهم بناء على الحال، وكونها زائدة على الذات مع كونها من صفات النفس ، الصفة النفسية، ما لا تكون زائدة على ذات الموصوف، وحينئذ يتوجه أن مفهوم لفظ الحقيقة والشيئية والوجود كلها زائدة على ذات الإنسان وإن أريد أنها ما لا تكون مفتقرة إلى ملاحظة أمر خارج مغاير للموصوف، أي ما لا يكون إضافياً، يشكل التماثل؛ لأنه إضافي. وإن أريد أنه لا يعلل بغير الذات، فيشكل بالوجود، وإن أريد أنه لا يكون مغايراً للذات في الخارج يتناول سائر الاعتبارات . قوله : ( كالتحيز) فإن التوصيف به يحتاج إلى ملاحظة الحيز والحدوث، فإنه يحتاج إلى ملاحظة العدم، وليس شيء منهما منتزعاً من نفس الإنسان مثلاً . قوله : ( تدل على الذات ) أي نفسه دلالة اللازم على الملزوم . قوله دون معنى زائد أي خارج عنها، أشار إلى أن ما يدل على جزء الذات داخل في الصفة النفسية. قوله : ( وكونها زائدة على الذات) فلا يكون منتزعاً من نفس الذات، فتحتاج في الوصف به إلى ملاحظة أمر سوى الذات، فلا يصدق التعريف عليها. قوله : (مع كونها من صفات النفس أما إذا كانت معللة بالصفات الحقيقية، فهي داخلة في الصفة المعنوية . قوله : ( ما لا يحتاج وصف الشيء به إلى تعقل أمر زائد قيل : أي غير هذه الصفة، وقيل: الكلام مبني على أن الوصف عين الماهية، وهو الأظهر. قوله : ( والوجود) فإن قلت : وصف الممكن بالوجود يحتاج إلى تعقل الفاعل الموجد، قلت : ممنوع نعم وجوده في نفس الأمر من الفاعل لكن لا توقف في التعقل . قوله : ( كالتحيز والحدوث) فإن الأول زائد على ذات الجوهر؛ لأنه باعتبار الجسمية، وتعقله . والثاني زائد على ذات الحادث؛ لأنه باعتبار العدم السابق وتعقله . واعلم أن عد الحدوث صفة معنوية مخالف لما في أبكار الأفكار حيث صرح في بحث المتخالفين في موضعين بأن الحدوث من الصفات النفسية. قوله : ( بناء على الحال ، وكونها زائدة على الذات من الأحوال ما يصح خلو الموصوف عنها، كعالمية زيد مثلاً، لكن الأحوال التي جعلوها من الصفات النفسية على هذا التفسير هي الأحوال اللازمة، كما سيشير إليه الشارح عن قريب .
The essential attribute (al-ṣifa al-nafsiyya) is that whose attribution to a thing does not require conceiving an additional matter beyond it, such as humanity, reality, existence, and thingness for man. Its opposite is the meaningful attributes (al-ṣifāt al-maʿnawiyya) which, in attributing them, require conceiving an additional matter beyond the essence of the described, such as spatial occupation (al-taḥayyuz) and temporal origination (al-ḥudūth). In other words: the essential attribute indicates the essence without an additional meaning, while the meaningful indicates an additional meaning beyond the essence. Some said, based on the state (al-ḥāl) and its being additional to the essence while being among the attributes of the essence: the essential attribute is that which is not additional to the essence of the described. Then it follows that the concept of the words reality, thingness, and existence are all additional to the essence of man. If it is intended that they are not dependent on observing an external matter different from the described, i.e., they are not relational, then likeness (al-tamāthul) poses a problem because it is relational. If it is intended that it is not caused by other than the essence, then existence poses a problem. If it is intended that it is not different from the essence in the external, it includes all considerations. His saying: (like spatial occupation) because describing by it requires observing spatial occupation, and temporal origination requires observing non-existence, and neither is abstracted from the essence of man himself, for example. His saying: (indicates the essence) i.e., itself, by the implication of the necessary to the necessitated. His saying: without an additional meaning, i.e., external to it; he indicated that what indicates a part of the essence is included in the essential attribute. His saying: (and its being additional to the essence) so it is not abstracted from the essence itself, thus describing by it requires observing something other than the essence, so the definition does not apply to it. His saying: (while being among the attributes of the essence) but if they are caused by true attributes (al-ṣifāt al-ḥaqīqiyya), they are included in the meaningful attribute. His saying: (that whose attribution to a thing does not require conceiving an additional matter) it was said: i.e., other than this attribute, and it was said: the discussion is based on the attribute being identical to the quiddity (al-māhiyya), and that is the more apparent. His saying: (and existence) if you say: describing the possible by existence requires conceiving the efficient cause that brings into existence, I say: it is denied; indeed its existence in reality is from the agent, but there is no dependence in conception. His saying: (like spatial occupation and temporal origination) for the first is additional to the essence of the substance because it is by virtue of corporeality and its conception; and the second is additional to the essence of the originated because it is by virtue of the preceding non-existence and its conception. Know that counting temporal origination as a meaningful attribute contradicts what is in Abkār al-Afkār, where it is explicitly stated in two places in the discussion of the disputants that temporal origination is among the essential attributes. His saying: (based on the state, and its being additional to the essence) from among the states (al-aḥwāl) is that from which the described can be free, like the knowledge of Zayd, for example, but the states that they made among the essential attributes according to this interpretation are the necessary states (al-aḥwāl al-lāzima), as the commentator will indicate shortly.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the two types of attributes: the essential attribute (al-ṣifa al-nafsiyya) and the meaningful attribute (al-ṣifa al-maʿnawiyya). The author begins by giving the primary definition: an essential attribute is one whose attribution does not require conceiving an additional matter beyond the thing itself. Examples given are humanity, reality, existence, and thingness for man. In contrast, meaningful attributes require conceiving something additional beyond the essence of the described, like spatial occupation and temporality. The author then provides an alternative phrasing: the essential attribute indicates the essence without an additional meaning, while the meaningful indicates an additional meaning. He then discusses a view based on the concept of 'state' (al-ḥāl) and its being additional to the essence while still being an attribute of the essence. According to this, the essential attribute is that which is not additional to the essence. This leads to objections: the concepts of reality, thingness, and existence are all additional to the essence of man. The author examines possible interpretations of 'not additional' and shows that each has problems. For instance, if 'not additional' means not relational, then likeness (al-tamāthul) poses a problem because it is relational. If it means not caused by another, existence is problematic. If it means not different in external existence, it becomes too broad. The commentary then explains the examples: spatial occupation requires conceiving space, temporality requires conceiving non-existence, and neither is abstracted from the essence. The commentary also notes a disagreement: counting temporality as a meaningful attribute contradicts what is in Abkār al-Afkār, where it is considered essential. Finally, the commentary clarifies that states (aḥwāl) that are necessary (lāzima) can be included in essential attributes according to this interpretation.

الصفة المعنوية
الوجود
الحدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many students think existence is a meaningful attribute because it depends on a creator, but here it is essential because describing something as existent does not require conceiving an additional concept beyond the thing itself (though later there is a discussion).
Correction: According to the primary definition, existence is essential because saying 'the thing exists' does not add a new concept; it is the thing's own reality.

Checkpoint
According to the first definition, which of the following is an example of an essential attribute (al-ṣifa al-nafsiyya)?
A) Spatial occupation (al-taḥayyuz)
B) Humanity (al-insāniyya)
C) Temporal origination (al-ḥudūth)
D) Knowledge (al-ʿilm)

Key Takeaway
Essential attributes are intrinsic to the essence; meaningful attributes require an extra conceptual element.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat your own existence as an essential fact of who you are, or do you sometimes doubt it? How does knowing that existence is an essential attribute (not an added concept) reshape your certainty in Allah's existence? Commit to reflecting daily on Allah's essential existence as the foundation of all reality.
?
When you describe Allah with attributes like 'alive' or 'knowing', do you secretly think of them as add-ons to His essence, or do you affirm that they simply are His essence without separation? What would change if you truly internalized that for Allah, every attribute is essential? This week, before each prayer, pause and say: 'Allah's attributes are His essence, not separate additions.'
?
The passage contrasts essential and meaningful attributes using created examples. But applied to Allah, all His attributes are essential—yet you still conceive them as separate. What does this tension reveal about the limits of your mind, and how can that lead you to greater humility before His majesty? Write down one way you can remind yourself of this when you think about Allah's names and attributes.

Divine Attributes
intermediate

The Alternative Definition and Its Interpretations
Sanusi discusses the alternative definition based on al-hal and analyses three interpretations of 'not additional'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the alternative definition based on 'al-hal' and the difficulties in interpreting 'not additional'.

Core Idea
Defining 'not additional' is tricky; each interpretation faces a counterexample.

The author presents an alternative definition that considers the attribute's relation to the essence as a 'state' (hal). This leads to several attempts to clarify what 'not additional' means, but each runs into problems. This lesson examines those issues.

Guided Path
1
Read the alternative definition
Focus on the sentence: 'Some said, based on the state... the essential attribute is that which is not additional to the essence.' Understand the shift.
This definition makes essential attributes those that are not extra to the essence.
2
Identify the three interpretations
The author gives three possible meanings of 'not additional': (1) not relational, (2) not caused by another, (3) not externally distinct. Write them down.
3
Note the counterexamples
For each interpretation, a problem arises: likeness (tamathul) for relational, existence for caused, and the third is too broad. Understand why.
These counterexamples show the definition is not straightforward.
4
Reflect on the overall point
The author is showing that defining 'essential' as 'not additional' is ambiguous and each interpretation fails. This prepares for the later clarification.

الصفة النفسية ما لا يحتاج وصف الشيء به إلى تعقل أمر زائد عليه كالإنسانية، والحقيقة، والوجود، والشيئية للإنسان، وتقابلها الصفات المعنوية التي تحتاج في الوصف بها إلى تعقل أمر زائد على ذات الموصوف كالتحيز والحدوث، وبعبارة أخرى : الصفة النفسية تدل على الذات دون معنى زائد عليها والمعنوية ما تدل على معنى زائد على الذات وقال بعضهم بناء على الحال، وكونها زائدة على الذات مع كونها من صفات النفس ، الصفة النفسية، ما لا تكون زائدة على ذات الموصوف، وحينئذ يتوجه أن مفهوم لفظ الحقيقة والشيئية والوجود كلها زائدة على ذات الإنسان وإن أريد أنها ما لا تكون مفتقرة إلى ملاحظة أمر خارج مغاير للموصوف، أي ما لا يكون إضافياً، يشكل التماثل؛ لأنه إضافي. وإن أريد أنه لا يعلل بغير الذات، فيشكل بالوجود، وإن أريد أنه لا يكون مغايراً للذات في الخارج يتناول سائر الاعتبارات . قوله : ( كالتحيز) فإن التوصيف به يحتاج إلى ملاحظة الحيز والحدوث، فإنه يحتاج إلى ملاحظة العدم، وليس شيء منهما منتزعاً من نفس الإنسان مثلاً . قوله : ( تدل على الذات ) أي نفسه دلالة اللازم على الملزوم . قوله دون معنى زائد أي خارج عنها، أشار إلى أن ما يدل على جزء الذات داخل في الصفة النفسية. قوله : ( وكونها زائدة على الذات) فلا يكون منتزعاً من نفس الذات، فتحتاج في الوصف به إلى ملاحظة أمر سوى الذات، فلا يصدق التعريف عليها. قوله : (مع كونها من صفات النفس أما إذا كانت معللة بالصفات الحقيقية، فهي داخلة في الصفة المعنوية . قوله : ( ما لا يحتاج وصف الشيء به إلى تعقل أمر زائد قيل : أي غير هذه الصفة، وقيل: الكلام مبني على أن الوصف عين الماهية، وهو الأظهر. قوله : ( والوجود) فإن قلت : وصف الممكن بالوجود يحتاج إلى تعقل الفاعل الموجد، قلت : ممنوع نعم وجوده في نفس الأمر من الفاعل لكن لا توقف في التعقل . قوله : ( كالتحيز والحدوث) فإن الأول زائد على ذات الجوهر؛ لأنه باعتبار الجسمية، وتعقله . والثاني زائد على ذات الحادث؛ لأنه باعتبار العدم السابق وتعقله . واعلم أن عد الحدوث صفة معنوية مخالف لما في أبكار الأفكار حيث صرح في بحث المتخالفين في موضعين بأن الحدوث من الصفات النفسية. قوله : ( بناء على الحال ، وكونها زائدة على الذات من الأحوال ما يصح خلو الموصوف عنها، كعالمية زيد مثلاً، لكن الأحوال التي جعلوها من الصفات النفسية على هذا التفسير هي الأحوال اللازمة، كما سيشير إليه الشارح عن قريب .
The essential attribute (al-ṣifa al-nafsiyya) is that whose attribution to a thing does not require conceiving an additional matter beyond it, such as humanity, reality, existence, and thingness for man. Its opposite is the meaningful attributes (al-ṣifāt al-maʿnawiyya) which, in attributing them, require conceiving an additional matter beyond the essence of the described, such as spatial occupation (al-taḥayyuz) and temporal origination (al-ḥudūth). In other words: the essential attribute indicates the essence without an additional meaning, while the meaningful indicates an additional meaning beyond the essence. Some said, based on the state (al-ḥāl) and its being additional to the essence while being among the attributes of the essence: the essential attribute is that which is not additional to the essence of the described. Then it follows that the concept of the words reality, thingness, and existence are all additional to the essence of man. If it is intended that they are not dependent on observing an external matter different from the described, i.e., they are not relational, then likeness (al-tamāthul) poses a problem because it is relational. If it is intended that it is not caused by other than the essence, then existence poses a problem. If it is intended that it is not different from the essence in the external, it includes all considerations. His saying: (like spatial occupation) because describing by it requires observing spatial occupation, and temporal origination requires observing non-existence, and neither is abstracted from the essence of man himself, for example. His saying: (indicates the essence) i.e., itself, by the implication of the necessary to the necessitated. His saying: without an additional meaning, i.e., external to it; he indicated that what indicates a part of the essence is included in the essential attribute. His saying: (and its being additional to the essence) so it is not abstracted from the essence itself, thus describing by it requires observing something other than the essence, so the definition does not apply to it. His saying: (while being among the attributes of the essence) but if they are caused by true attributes (al-ṣifāt al-ḥaqīqiyya), they are included in the meaningful attribute. His saying: (that whose attribution to a thing does not require conceiving an additional matter) it was said: i.e., other than this attribute, and it was said: the discussion is based on the attribute being identical to the quiddity (al-māhiyya), and that is the more apparent. His saying: (and existence) if you say: describing the possible by existence requires conceiving the efficient cause that brings into existence, I say: it is denied; indeed its existence in reality is from the agent, but there is no dependence in conception. His saying: (like spatial occupation and temporal origination) for the first is additional to the essence of the substance because it is by virtue of corporeality and its conception; and the second is additional to the essence of the originated because it is by virtue of the preceding non-existence and its conception. Know that counting temporal origination as a meaningful attribute contradicts what is in Abkār al-Afkār, where it is explicitly stated in two places in the discussion of the disputants that temporal origination is among the essential attributes. His saying: (based on the state, and its being additional to the essence) from among the states (al-aḥwāl) is that from which the described can be free, like the knowledge of Zayd, for example, but the states that they made among the essential attributes according to this interpretation are the necessary states (al-aḥwāl al-lāzima), as the commentator will indicate shortly.

Further Clarifications and a Disagreement on Temporal Origination
Sanusi explains the examples and notes a contradiction with another text, then clarifies based on necessary states.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the details regarding spatial occupation and temporality, and the disagreement about whether temporality is essential or meaningful.

Core Idea
Temporal origination may be considered an essential attribute by some scholars, contrary to the earlier example.

The commentary delves deeper into the examples of spatial occupation and temporal origination, clarifying why they require additional concepts. It also notes a disagreement: in another work, temporal origination is listed as an essential attribute. This lesson explores that nuance.

Guided Path
1
Read the commentary on tahayyuz and huduth
The passage explains why spatial occupation and temporal origination are meaningful: they require conceiving space and non-existence respectively.
Notice that these are not abstracted from the essence itself.
2
Understand the classification of states
The passage distinguishes between attributes that are caused by true attributes (meaningful) and those that are not. Also, it mentions that states considered essential are necessary states (lazima).
3
Examine the disagreement
The author notes that in Abkār al-Afkār, temporal origination is counted as an essential attribute, contradicting the example here. Understand the reason for this difference.
The resolution involves necessary states.
4
Reflect on the overall lesson
The classification of attributes is not always straightforward; context and criteria matter.

الصفة الحقيقية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that spatial occupation is always a meaningful attribute, but the passage doesn't dispute that; it's the classification of huduth that is debated.
Correction: Spatial occupation is consistently meaningful; the debate is about temporal origination, which some scholars consider essential.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, counting temporal origination as a meaningful attribute contradicts which text?
A) Al-Mawaqif
B) Abkār al-Afkār
C) Al-Iqtisad
D) Al-Muhassal

Key Takeaway
Spatial occupation and temporal origination are meaningful attributes, but temporal origination's classification is debated; the resolution involves necessary states.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you learn that even great scholars like al-Āmidī disagreed on whether temporal origination is an essential or meaningful attribute, do you feel a sense of awe at the depth of their inquiry, or does it tempt you to think such debates are irrelevant? What step can you take to honor the precision of Islamic theology in your own learning?
?
The passage states that existence (wujūd) does not depend on conceiving the agent for its conception. Does this challenge or confirm your own certainty in Allah's existence? If you ever experience doubt, what specific insight from this lesson can you anchor yourself with?
?
The concept of 'necessary states' (aḥwāl lāzima) is used to resolve a contradiction. Can you identify an area of your faith where you have accepted a simplistic view without appreciating the nuance? What will you do to seek a deeper understanding of that matter?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
12 min
Alternative Definition of Essential Attribute and the Concept of Likeness
Defines essential attribute and presents two definitions of likeness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the alternative definition of the essential attribute and how it leads to two equivalent definitions of 'two likenesses' (al-mithlān) based on shared necessary, possible, and impossible attributes.

Core Idea
Likeness is defined through sharing in what is necessary, possible, and impossible.

This passage refines the definition of an essential attribute as that which cannot be validly thought to be removed from its subject. It then applies this concept to define what it means for two things to be alike. The author presents two formulations of likeness, both revolving around the threefold division of rational judgments: necessary, possible, and impossible. Understanding this foundation is key to later discussions on divine attributes and the uniqueness of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the two definitions of likeness.
2
Identify the definition of essential attribute
The passage begins with a definition: the essential attribute is that which it is not valid to suppose its removal. Understand the nuance: 'not valid' means the supposition is false, not inconceivable.
3
Understand the threefold division
The author says sharing in essential attributes entails sharing in what is necessary, possible, and impossible. These are the three rational judgments that form the basis of kalam reasoning.
4
Compare the two definitions of likeness
The first definition says two likenesses share what is necessary, possible, and impossible for them. The second says one takes the place of the other in all such judgments. Both are equivalent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصفة النفسية ما لا يصح توهم ارتفاعها عن موصوفها والمعنوية ما يقابلها. ( ويلزمها ) أي يلزم المشاركة في الصفات النفسية ( المشاركة فيما يجب، ويمكن، ويمتنع ، ولذلك قد يعرف به فيقال : المثلان هما الموجودان اللذان يشارك كل منهما الآخر فيما يجب له ويمكن ويمتنع . ( وقد يقال ) : بعبارة أخرى المثلان : ( ما يسد أحدهما مسد الآخر في الأحكام الواجبة والجائزة والممتنعة جميعاً، ولأن الصفة النفسية كما عرفت ( ما يعود إلى نفس الذات لا إلى معنى زائد ) على الذات، ( فالتماثل ) من الصفات النفسية، لأنه (أمر ذاتي ليس لمعنى زائد ) . يعني أن التماثل قوله : ( ما لا يصح) أي يكون تصور ارتفاعها عن الموصوف باطلاً غير مطابق، فالصحة في مقابلة البطلان لا بمعنى الجواز، فلا يرد أن توهم ارتفاع كل صفة عن موصوفها ممكن، إنما المحال ارتفاع المتوهم . قوله : ( فيما يجب ويمكن (ويمتنع أي بالنظر إلى ذاتهما فلا برد أن الصفات منحصرة في الأقسام الثلاثة فيلزم منه اشتراك المثلين في جميع الصفات فيرتفع التعدد عنهما . قوله : ( في الأحكام الواجبة إلخ ) أي بالنظر إلى ذاتهما وتلازم التعريفات الثلاثة ظاهر بعد التأمل. قوله : ( ولأن الصفة النفسية إلخ ) علة لقوله : فالتماثل أمر ذاتي إلخ والجملة عطف على قوله وهما الموجودان وأصل الكلام، فالتماثل أمر ذاتي لأن الصفة النفسية إلا أنه لما قدم الدليل وصار الفاء لمجرد ترتب المدلول على الدليل زاد الواو العاطفة . قوله : (ما يعود إلى نفس الذات إلخ) أي يكون منتزعاً من نفسها من غير مدخلية أمر خارج عنها . قوله : ( من الصفات النفسية إلخ) قدر الخبر، وجعل ما هو الخبر في المتن تعليلاً له إشارة إلى أن في المتن اختصاراً بإقامة سبب الخبر مقامه . قوله : ( ما لا يصح توهم ارتفاعها عن موصوفها أي ارتفاعها المتوهم، فلا ينافي ما سبق من إمكان توهم ارتفاع اللازم عن الملزوم ولك أن تقول الصحة هاهنا مقابل البطلان والمعنى: ما لا يبطل توهم ارتفاعها أي لا يكون ذلك التوهم على طبق الواقع . قوله: (فيما يجب ويمكن ويمتنع لعل المراد فيما يجب ويمكن ويمتنع بحسب الماهية، وإلا جاز أن يستند بعض هذه الأمور إلى الشخص المخصوص فتأمل . قوله : ( ولأن الصفة النفسية المتبادر من السياق أنه تعليل لكون التماثل من الصفات النفسية، ولذا غير الشارح أسلوب المصنف، وقدر الخبر لقوله فالتماثل، وجعل قوله : لأنه أمر ذاتي تعليلا لتفرع كون التماثل من الصفات النفسية على كونها ما يعود إلى نفس الذات، لكن تفريع قوله : فهو صفة نفسية على كون التماثل غير معلل بأمر زائد على الذات إنما يظهر في الجملة على تقدير أن يراد بالأمر الزائد في تعريف الصفة النفسية غير تلك الصفة؛ إذ لو بني الكلام على أن الوصف عين الماهية لم يلزم من تعليل التماثل بنفس الذات لا بغيرها كونه نفس الذات، بل لم يصح، فلا يلزم كونه صفة نفسية فتأمل .
The essential attribute is that which it is not valid to suppose its removal from its described, and the meaningful is its opposite. (And it necessitates) i.e., sharing in essential attributes necessitates (sharing in what is necessary, possible, and impossible. Therefore it may be defined by it, and it is said: the two likenesses (al-mithlān) are the two existents each of which shares with the other what is necessary for it, possible, and impossible. (And it may be said) in other words: the two likenesses are (that which one of them takes the place of the other in all obligatory, permissible, and impossible judgments. And because the essential attribute, as you know, (is that which goes back to the essence itself, not to an additional meaning) beyond the essence, (so likeness) is among the essential attributes, because it is (an essential matter not due to an additional meaning). That is, that likeness... His saying: (that which it is not valid) i.e., conceiving its removal from the described is false and not corresponding [to reality]; validity is in contrast to falsehood, not in the sense of permissibility, so it is not objected that supposing the removal of every attribute from its described is possible; only the supposed removal is impossible. His saying: (in what is necessary, possible, and impossible) i.e., with respect to their essences, so it is not objected that attributes are confined to three divisions, which would necessitate the two likenesses sharing all attributes, thereby eliminating their multiplicity. His saying: (in obligatory, etc.) i.e., with respect to their essences, and the mutual correlation of the three definitions is apparent after reflection. His saying: (And because the essential attribute, etc.) is a cause for his saying: so likeness is an essential matter, etc., and the sentence is conjoined to his saying: and they are the two existents, and the original wording is: so likeness is an essential matter because the essential attribute, except that when the proof was presented and the faa' became merely for the sequence of the meaning upon the proof, he added the conjunctive waw. His saying: (that which goes back to the essence itself, etc.) i.e., it is abstracted from itself without the intervention of an external matter. His saying: (from among the essential attributes, etc.) the predicate is supplied, and making what is the predicate in the text a cause for it indicates that there is an abbreviation in the text by substituting the cause of the predicate for it. His saying: (that which it is not valid to suppose its removal from its described) i.e., its supposed removal, so it does not contradict what preceded regarding the possibility of supposing the removal of the necessary from the necessitated. But you may say: validity here is opposite to falsehood, and the meaning is: that whose supposed removal is not false, i.e., that supposition does not correspond to reality. His saying: (in what is necessary, possible, and impossible) perhaps the meaning is in what is necessary, possible, and impossible according to the quiddity, otherwise it is possible that some of these matters are attributed to the particular person, so reflect. His saying: (And because the essential attribute) what is understood from the context is that it is a cause for likeness being among the essential attributes, and therefore the commentator changed the author's style, supplied the predicate for his saying 'so likeness', and made his saying 'because it is an essential matter' a cause for the dependency of likeness being among the essential attributes upon its being that which goes back to the essence itself. But the dependency of his saying 'so it is an essential attribute' upon likeness not being caused by an additional matter beyond the essence appears only in general on the assumption that by 'additional matter' in the definition of the essential attribute is meant other than that attribute; for if the discussion were based on the attribute being identical to the quiddity, it would not follow from likeness being caused by the essence itself and not by another that it is the essence itself; rather it would not be valid, so it would not follow that it is an essential attribute. So reflect.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage presents an alternative definition of the essential attribute (al-ṣifa al-nafsiyya): it is that which it is not valid to suppose its removal from its described. The meaningful attribute is its opposite. The author then discusses likeness (al-tamāthul) and its connection to essential attributes. He states that sharing in essential attributes necessitates sharing in what is necessary, possible, and impossible for the things. Therefore, two likenesses (al-mithlān) are defined as two existents each of which shares with the other in all necessary, possible, and impossible matters with respect to their essences. Another definition: one can take the place of the other in all obligatory, permissible, and impossible judgments. The argument is that because the essential attribute goes back to the essence itself and not to an additional meaning, likeness is an essential attribute because it is an essential matter not due to an additional meaning. The commentary then explains the wording: 'not valid' means that conceiving removal is false, not that it is impossible to conceive; validity is in contrast to falsehood. The phrase 'in what is necessary, possible, and impossible' refers to the essences, not external accidental attributes. The commentary also clarifies that the definitions of likeness are interrelated. Finally, the commentary delves into the logical structure of the proof, noting that the commentator altered the author's style to make the reasoning clear: since the essential attribute is that which goes back to the essence, and likeness is not caused by something additional, it follows that likeness is an essential attribute. However, this depends on the interpretation that 'additional matter' in the definition means other than the attribute itself; if the attribute is identical to the quiddity, the reasoning may not hold.

Key Terms
الصفة النفسية
المثلان
الواجب
الممكن
الممتنع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'not valid to suppose removal' means it is impossible to conceive of the removal.
Correction: The passage clarifies that 'not valid' means the supposition is false, not that it is inconceivable. It is possible to conceive of removal, but that conception does not correspond to reality.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does sharing in essential attributes necessitate?
A) Sharing in spatial occupation
B) Sharing in what is necessary, possible, and impossible
C) Sharing in existence
D) Sharing in temporal origination

Key Takeaway
The essential attribute is defined by the impossibility of validly supposing its removal, and likeness is defined by complete agreement in necessary, possible, and impossible attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever, in your heart, imagine God as similar to something you have experienced, even if you verbally deny any likeness? How does the precise definition of 'likeness' in this lesson—complete agreement in necessary, possible, and impossible—expose any hidden assumptions you might hold? What will you actively do to uproot such thoughts from your heart this week?
?
The essential attribute is defined as that whose removal cannot be validly supposed. Think of an attribute of God you struggle to internalize, like His eternal mercy or justice. Does your soul truly feel the impossibility of its removal from Him, or do you sometimes doubt it? What concrete step can you take today to strengthen your certainty that His attributes are ever-present?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
10 min
Proof that Likeness is an Essential Attribute
Provides the proof that likeness is an essential attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that likeness (al-tamāthul) is itself an essential attribute, based on the definition of essential attribute as that which belongs to the essence without additional meaning.

Core Idea
Likeness is an essential attribute because it is based on the essence itself, not on extra meanings.

Having defined essential attributes and the nature of likeness, the author now demonstrates that the very relation of likeness between two things qualifies as an essential attribute. This is a subtle but crucial point, as it impacts how we understand divine attributes and the uniqueness of Allah. The proof relies on the distinction between attributes that go back to the essence itself and those that require an additional meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Focus on the logical flow from the definition to the conclusion.
2
Understand the definition of essential attribute
The passage recalls that an essential attribute is that which goes back to the essence itself, not to an additional meaning. This is the key premise.
3
See how likeness fits
The author argues that likeness is an essential matter not due to an additional meaning. Therefore, it falls under the definition of an essential attribute.
4
Review the commentary on the proof structure
The commentary clarifies that the proof is abbreviated: the author presented the cause (the definition of essential attribute) but left the conclusion implied. The commentator restructured it to show the logical connection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Likeness is a relative attribute that depends on an external relation between two things.
Correction: The passage argues that likeness is an essential attribute based on the essences themselves, not on an additional relational meaning. It is intrinsic to the things being compared.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for considering likeness an essential attribute?
A) It is a common term used in everyday language
B) It is an essential matter not due to an additional meaning
C) It is derived from the concept of similarity
D) It is a necessary attribute of all existents

Key Takeaway
Likeness is an essential attribute because it is an essential matter that does not depend on an additional meaning beyond the essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Before this lesson, did you think that 'likeness' between two things required an outside relation? How does the proof that it is an essential attribute change the way you think about God's attributes being identical to His essence? Write down one practical implication of this for your understanding of tawḥīd.
?
If likeness is an essential attribute, then it cannot be separated from the essence. Reflect on what this means for the way you understand the relationship between God and His attributes. Is there any attribute you previously considered separate? How does this affect your worship and reliance on God?
?
The passage defines an essential attribute as 'that which goes back to the essence itself.' Consider your own self: what are the essential aspects of your identity that are not added? How does recognizing pure essence without additions bring you closer to understanding God's oneness?

Al-Qāḍī's Two Views on Tamāthul: Essential or Superadded?
Discusses al-Qāḍī's two positions on tamāthul: superadded vs. essential.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Qāḍī's two conflicting positions on tamāthul and why one view considers it an essential attribute through the sufficiency of assuming the other.

Core Idea
Tamāthul can be essential without an actual other, relying on possibility alone.

Al-Qāḍī al-Bāqillānī, a leading Ash'arī theologian, was hesitant about whether tamāthul (similarity) is an added attribute or an essential one. This passage presents his two views, showing a shift from seeing tamāthul as dependent on actual existence to being firmly rooted in the essence's own possibility. Understanding this nuance clarifies how attributes of genera are independent of external causes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the two positions of al-Qāḍī. Notice the key terms: zā'id (additional), taqdīr (assumption), and ṣifāt al-ajnās (attributes of genera).
The passage is concise; pay attention to the shift in reasoning.
2
Identify the two positions
Find where al-Qāḍī first says tamāthul is zā'id (superadded) and then says it is not. Mark the phrases that indicate each view.
The first view uses 'zā'id' and 'yakhluu 'anhu bi-taqdīr 'adam khalq al-ghayr'. The second uses 'ghayr zā'id' and 'yakfī fī ittiṣāf... taqdīr al-ghayr'.
3
Understand the supporting argument
Read the final sentence where al-Qāḍī supports the second view by saying attributes of genera are not caused by an external thing. This makes tamāthul dependent on possibility, not actual existence.
The key phrase: 'lā tu'allalu bi-l-ghayr ittifāqan'.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this matters for divine attributes: if tamāthul is essential, then self-subsisting attributes need not rely on external creation. This aligns with the Ash'arī concept of necessary attributes.
Connects to the broader discussion of essential vs. superadded attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما عند مثبتي الأحوال منا كالقاضي ففيه تردد، إذ قال تارة أنه زائد على الصفات النفسية، ويخلو عنه بتقدير عدم خلق الغير فلا يكون من الصفات والأحوال اللازمة. وقال أخرى: التماثل غير زائد على الصفات النفسية، بل هو منها ويكفي في اتصاف الشيء بالتماثل تقدير الغير فيكون الشيء حال انفراده عن غيره في الوجود متصفاً بالتماثل غير خال عنه، فيكون من الأحوال اللازمة للذات. ثم أيد كون تقدير الغير كافياً في الاتصاف بالتماثل بقوله: فإن صفات الأجناس، ومن جملتها التماثل، لا تعلل بالغير اتفاقاً، فلا يكون التماثل موقوفاً على وجود الغير تحقيقاً.
And as for with the upholders of states among us, like al-Qāḍī, there is hesitation concerning it, for he said once that it is additional to the essential attributes, and its subject is devoid of it assuming the non-creation of the other, so it is not among the necessary attributes and states. And he said another time: tamāthul is not additional to the essential attributes, but rather it is among them, and the assumption of the other suffices for the description of the thing with tamāthul, so the thing when alone by itself in existence is described with tamāthul, not devoid of it, so it is among the necessary states of the essence. Then he supported the sufficiency of the assumption of the other for the description with tamāthul by saying: for the attributes of genera, among which is tamāthul, are not caused by the other, by agreement, so tamāthul is not dependent on the existence of the other actually.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage examines the position of al-Qāḍī (Abū Bakr al-Bāqillānī) regarding whether tamāthul is an essential attribute or a superadded attribute. It first notes that al-Qāḍī is hesitant. On one occasion, he said that tamāthul is additional (zā'id) to the essential attributes, meaning it is not essential because if the other entity were not created, the thing would be devoid of tamāthul. Thus it is not a necessary attribute or state. On another occasion, he said that tamāthul is not additional but rather among the essential attributes, and the mere assumption (taqdīr) of the other is sufficient for the thing to be described with tamāthul. Even when alone, it is still described with tamāthul due to the possibility of another similar existing. Therefore, it is a necessary state of the essence. Al-Qāḍī supports this latter view by noting that attributes of genera, including tamāthul, are not caused by an external thing (al-ghayr) by agreement. Thus tamāthul does not depend on the actual existence of another, only on its possibility. This shows the nuance in defining tamāthul among the Ash‘arites.

أثبات الأحوال
زائد
تقدير الغير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think tamāthul requires an actually existing other entity to be described as similar.
Correction: The passage shows that al-Qāḍī argues tamāthul can be described by merely assuming the other (taqdīr al-ghayr), so actual existence is not needed.

Checkpoint
According to one of al-Qāḍī's positions, when is a thing described with tamāthul?
A) Only when another similar actually exists.
B) Even when alone, by assuming the other.
C) Only when both are created.
D) Never, as tamāthul is impossible.

Key Takeaway
Al-Qāḍī's final view is that tamāthul is an essential attribute, not dependent on actual existence, because attributes of genera are not caused by external things.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

What is one belief or practice that is true about your faith even when you are completely alone, needing no external validation? Will you commit to grounding your faith in that truth today, regardless of what others do?
?
Al-Qāḍī's argument relies on the principle that attributes of genera are not caused by the other. How often do you attribute your spiritual state to your environment or the people around you? What would it mean for your worship or character to be an essential attribute of your soul, not dependent on external circumstances? What step can you take this week to cultivate such an attribute?

Tamathul as a Psychological Attribute and Its Status
Discussion of tamathul as a psychological attribute and the dispute over its status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of tamathul as a psychological attribute and the disagreement among proponents of states regarding whether it is additional to psychological attributes or part of them.

Core Idea
The status of tamathul hinges on whether it requires actual existence of another or merely an estimated other.

This passage from Sharh al-Mawaqif defines tamathul (likeness) as a psychological attribute (ṣifa nafsiyya) and then presents the hesitation among those who hold the theory of states (aḥwāl), like al-Qadi. The central debate is whether tamathul is additional to psychological attributes (allowing it to be absent) or whether it is part of them (a necessary state). The resolution relies on the principle that genus attributes are not caused by an external existing thing, so only an estimated other suffices.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the definition of tamathul as a psychological attribute and the two positions of al-Qadi.
Pay attention to the parentheses and interjections, which indicate the author's commentary.
2
Identify the two positions
Find where al-Qadi says tamathul is 'additional' (zāʼid) and then 'not additional' (ghayr zāʼid). Understand the consequence for necessary states.
The first position makes tamathul contingent on the existence of another; the second makes it a necessary state.
3
Understand the supporting argument
Notice the argument that genus attributes are not caused by an external existing thing. This supports the second position that only an estimated other is needed.
This argument is key to resolving the hesitation.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this matters for divine attributes: if tamathul is a necessary state, it is inseparable from the essence, affecting how we think about God's attributes compared to others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الذات لا نفسها وليس معللاً بأمر زائد عليها، فهو صفة نفسية عندنا، ( وأما عند مثبتي الأحوال منا كالقاضي ففيه ) أي في كون التماثل من الصفات النفسية المفسرة على رأيه بالأحوال اللازمة التي يمتنع توهم ارتفاعها عن الذات . ( تردد، إذ قال تارة أنه ( أي التماثل ( زائد ) على الصفات النفسية، (ويخلو) موصوفه ( عنه بتقدير عدم خلق الغير فلا يكون من الصفات والأحوال اللازمة (و) قال (أخرى) : التماثل ( غير زائد ) على الصفات النفسية، بل هو منها ويكفي) في اتصاف ( الشيء بالتماثل ( تقدير (الغير فيكون الشيء حال انفراده عن غيره في الوجود متصفاً بالتماثل، غير خال عنه، فيكون من الأحوال اللازمة للذات ثم أيد كون تقدير الغير الاتصاف بالتماثل بقوله : (فإن صفات الأجناس، ومن جملتها التماثل ( لا تعلل بالغير أي بأمر موجود مغاير لمحلها ( اتفاقا ) ، فلا يكون التماثل موقوفاً على وجود الغير تحقيقاً. وأما تقديره فلا يضر.
The essence [is] not itself and is not caused by something additional to it, so it is a psychological attribute (ṣifa nafsiyya) according to us. (As for the upholders of states (aḥwāl) among us, like al-Qadi, there is hesitation) regarding tamathul (being among the psychological attributes explained, in his view, as necessary states whose removal from the essence cannot be imagined. (Hesitation), for he said sometimes: tamathul is additional to psychological attributes, and its described subject is devoid of it on the supposition of not creating another, so it is not among necessary attributes and states. And he said another time: tamathul is not additional to psychological attributes, but rather it is from them, and it suffices for a thing to be described with tamathul to suppose the other, so the thing, while isolated from others in existence, is described with tamathul, not devoid of it, thus it is among the necessary states of the essence. Then he supported that considering the other suffices for being described with tamathul by his saying: "Indeed, genus attributes, among which is tamathul, are not caused by the other", i.e., by an existing thing different from their locus, by agreement, so tamathul does not depend on the actual existence of the other. And as for considering it, that does not harm.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage defines tamathul (likeness) as a psychological attribute (sifa nafsiyya) that is not caused by anything external. It then discusses the disagreement among those who hold the theory of states (ahwal), such as al-Qadi. The disagreement is whether tamathul is additional to psychological attributes (in which case it can be absent if no other exists) or whether it is part of them (so it is a necessary state that always accompanies the essence). The argument for the latter is that it suffices to suppose the existence of another entity, not its actual existence, because genus attributes (like tamathul) are not caused by an external existing thing. Thus, tamathul does not depend on the actual existence of another; merely conceiving it is enough.

الصفات النفسية
الأحوال اللازمة
تقدير الغير

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that tamathul requires an actually existing other entity.
Correction: The passage clarifies that it only requires an estimated (taqdīr) other, because genus attributes are not caused by an external existing thing.

Checkpoint

B) Because tamathul is a psychological attribute and always exists.
C) Because the existence of another is impossible.
D) Because tamathul is not a real property.

Key Takeaway
Tamathul is a psychological attribute, and according to the stronger view, it suffices to suppose the existence of another for a thing to be described with tamathul.

Are you willing to accept that your core worth is not dependent on other people's presence or approval? What concrete step can you take this week to live out that truth?
